style="text-align:center">\n<table style="width:95%; background: transparent; text-align:center; margin:0 auto;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="text-align:center; border:0; padding-bottom:0"><div id="before-after"></div></td>\n<td style="text-align:center;border:0; padding-bottom:0;"><b>Succeeded by</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center; border:0;">\n</td>\n<td style="vertical-align:top; text-align:center;border:0;">\n<table style="width:92%; background:transparent; text-align:center; margin:0 auto; border:0;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle; text-align:right;"><a href="/wiki/Overseas_France" title="Overseas France">Overseas France</a>\n</td>\n<td style="border:0; padding:0; vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="" data-file-height="2" data-file-width="3" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d2/Blank.png" width="22"/>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>French colonial empire</b> constituted the overseas colonies, protectorates and <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">mandate</a> territories that came under French rule from the 16th century onward. A distinction is generally made<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (July 2018)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> between the "first colonial empire," that existed until 1814, by which time most of it had been lost, and the "second colonial empire", which began with the conquest of Algiers in 1830. The second colonial empire came to an end after the loss in later wars <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">of Indochina</a> (1954) and <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">Algeria</a> (1962), and relatively peaceful <a href="/wiki/Decolonisation_of_Africa" title="Decolonisation of Africa">decolonizations</a> elsewhere after 1960.\n</p><p>Competing with <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portugal</a>, the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">United Provinces</a> and later <a href="/wiki/English_overseas_possessions" title="English overseas possessions">England</a>, France began to establish colonies in <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">North America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">India</a> in the 17th century. A series of wars with Britain and others resulted in France losing nearly all of its conquests by 1814. France rebuilt a new empire mostly after 1850, concentrating chiefly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_African_colonies" title="French African colonies">in Africa</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">Indochina</a> and the South Pacific. Republicans, at first hostile to empire, only became supportive when <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a> started to build <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">their own colonial empire</a>. As it developed, the new empire took on roles of trade with France, especially supplying raw materials and purchasing manufactured items as well as lending prestige to the motherland and spreading French civilization and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">language</a> and the Catholic religion. It also provided manpower in the World Wars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A major goal was the &#8216;Mission civilisatrice&#8217; the mission to spread French culture, language and religion, and this proved successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup>  In 1884, the leading proponent of colonialism, <a href="/wiki/Jules_Ferry" title="Jules Ferry">Jules Ferry</a>, declared; "The higher races have a right over the lower races, they have a <a href="/wiki/Civilizing_mission" title="Civilizing mission">duty to civilize the inferior races</a>." Full citizenship rights &#8211; <i>assimilation</i> &#8211; were offered, although in reality "assimilation was always receding [and] the colonial populations treated like subjects not citizens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> France sent small numbers of settlers to its empire, contrary to Great Britain and previously Spain and Portugal, with the only notable exception of Algeria, where the <a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">French settlers</a> nonetheless always remained a small minority.\n</p><p>At its apex, it was one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">largest empires in history</a>. Including <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan France</a>, the total amount of land under French sovereignty reached 11,500,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,400,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) in 1920, with a population of 110 million people in 1939. In World War II, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_French" title="Free French">Free French</a> used the overseas colonies as bases from which they fought to liberate France. Historian Tony Chafer argues: "In an effort to restore its world-power status after the humiliation of defeat and occupation, France was eager to maintain its overseas empire at the end of the Second World War."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> However, after 1945 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-colonial_liberation_movements" title="Anti-colonial liberation movements">anti-colonial movements</a> began to challenge European authority. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_constitution" title="French constitution">French constitution</a> of 27 October 1946 (Fourth Republic), established the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a> which endured until 1958. Newer remnants of the colonial empire were integrated into France as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_departments_and_territories_of_France" title="Overseas departments and territories of France">overseas departments and territories</a> within the French Republic. These now total altogether 119,394&#160;km&#178; (46,098 sq. miles), which amounts to only 1% of the pre-1939 French colonial empire\'s area, with 2.7 million people living in them in 2013. By the 1970s, says <a href="/wiki/Robert_Aldrich_(historian)" title="Robert Aldrich (historian)">Robert Aldrich</a>, the last "vestiges of empire held little interest for the French." He argues, "Except for the traumatic decolonization of Algeria, however, what is remarkable is how few long-lasting effects on France the giving up of empire entailed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li Japan (1866&#8211;68)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#France_in_Indochina_and_the_Pacific_(1858&#8211;70)"><span class="tocnumber">2.6</span> <span class="tocnumber">2.7</span> <span class="toctext">Intervention in Syria and Lebanon (1860&#8211;61)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Algeria"><span class="tocnumber">2.10</span> <span class="toctext">French&#8211;British relations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#French&#8211;U.S._relations"><span class="tocnumber">2.11</span> <span class="toctext">French&#8211;U.S. relations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#1870&#8211;1939"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">1870&#8211;1939</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18"><a href="#Asia"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span tocsection-23"><a href="#World_War_II"><span class="tocnumber">3.6</span> <span class="toctext">World War II</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#Decolonization"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Decolonization</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Conflict"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Conflict</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#French_settlers"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">French settlers</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Notes_and_references"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Notes and references</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Policies_and_colonies"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Policies and colonies</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Decolonization_2"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">Decolonization</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Images_and_impact_on_France"><span class="tocnumber">8.3</span> <span class="toctext">Images and impact on France</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Historiography_and_memoir"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Historiography and memoir</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="First_French_colonial_empire">First French colonial empire</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: First French colonial empire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Americas">The Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png"><img alt="Global map of French colonial empire" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1420" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png/250px-131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png/375px-131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png/500px-131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:131Etendue_de_l%27Empire_Fran%C3%A7ais.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the first (green) and second (blue) French colonial empires</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_France_(orthographic_projection).svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/250px-New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/375px-New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/500px-New_France_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_France_(orthographic_projection).svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The French colonial empire in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> comprised <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Louisiana" title="French Louisiana">Louisiana</a>), <a href="/wiki/French_West_Indies" title="French West Indies">French West Indies</a> (including <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dominica" title="History of Dominica">Dominica</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Saint_Lucia" title="History of Saint Lucia">St. Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Grenada" title="History of Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Tobago" title="History of Tobago">Tobago</a> and other islands) and <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg/250px-Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg/375px-Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg/500px-Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_nouvelle_france.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French Northern America was known as \'Nouvelle France\' or New France</div></div></div>\n<p>During the 16th century, the <a href="/wiki/French_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="French colonization of the Americas">French colonization of the Americas</a> began. Excursions of <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_da_Verrazzano" title="Giovanni da Verrazzano">Giovanni da Verrazzano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Cartier" title="Jacques Cartier">Jacques Cartier</a> in the early 16th century, as well as the frequent voyages of French boats and fishermen to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Banks" title="Grand Banks">Grand Banks</a> off <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> throughout that century, were the precursors to the story of France\'s colonial expansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> But Spain\'s defense of its American monopoly, and the further distractions caused in France itself in the later 16th century by the <a href="/wiki/French_Wars_of_Religion" title="French Wars of Religion">French Wars of Religion</a>, prevented any constant efforts by France to settle colonies. Early French attempts to found colonies in Brazil, in 1555 at <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> ("<a href="/wiki/France_Antarctique" title="France Antarctique">France Antarctique</a>") and in Florida (including <a href="/wiki/Fort_Caroline" title="Fort Caroline">Fort Caroline</a> in 1562), and in 1612 at <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Lu%C3%ADs,_Maranh%C3%A3o" title="S&#227;o Lu&#237;s, Maranh&#227;o">S&#227;o Lu&#237;s</a> ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/France_%C3%89quinoxiale" title="France &#201;quinoxiale">France &#201;quinoxiale</a>"), were not successful, due to a lack of official interest and to Portuguese and Spanish vigilance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The story of France\'s colonial empire truly began on 27 July 1605, with the foundation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitation_at_Port-Royal" title="Habitation at Port-Royal">Port Royal</a> in the colony of <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a> in North America, in what is now <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, Canada. A few years later, in 1608, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samuel_De_Champlain" title="Samuel De Champlain">Samuel De Champlain</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">Quebec</a>, which was to become the capital of the enormous, but sparsely settled, fur-trading colony of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> (also called Canada).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup>\n</p><p>New France had a rather small population, which resulted from more emphasis being placed on the fur trade rather than agricultural settlements. Due to this emphasis, the French relied heavily on creating friendly contacts with the local First Nations community. Without the appetite of New England for land, and by relying solely on Aboriginals to supply them with fur at the trading posts, the French composed a complex series of military, commercial, and diplomatic connections. These became the most enduring alliances between the French and the First Nation community. The French were, however, under pressure from religious orders to convert them to Catholicism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Through alliances with various Native American tribes, the French were able to exert a loose control over much of the North American continent. Areas of French settlement were generally limited to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> Valley. Prior to the establishment of the 1663 <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Council_of_New_France" title="Sovereign Council of New France">Sovereign Council</a>, the territories of New France were developed as <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantile colonies</a>. It is only after the arrival of intendant <a href="/wiki/Jean_Talon" title="Jean Talon">Jean Talon</a> in 1665 that France gave its American colonies the proper means to develop population colonies comparable to that of the British. Acadia itself was lost to the British in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht_(1713)" title="Treaty of Utrecht (1713)">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713. Back in France there was relatively little interest in colonialism, which concentrated rather on dominance within Europe, and for most of its history, New France was far behind the <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North American</a> colonies in both population and economic development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1699, French territorial claims in North America expanded still further, with the foundation of <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">Louisiana</a> in the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a>. The extensive trading network throughout the region connected to Canada through the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">Great Lakes</a>, was maintained through a vast system of fortifications, many of them centred in the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Country" title="Illinois Country">Illinois Country</a> and in present-day Arkansas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1700" decoding="async" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg/250px-1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg/375px-1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg/500px-1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1767_Colonies_Fran%C3%A7ois_12_Diniers_with_RF_Counterstamp.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1767 Louis XV <i>Colonies Fran&#231;oises</i> (West Indies) 12 Diniers copper Sous (w/1793 "RF" counterstamp)</div></div></div><p>As the French empire in North America grew, the French also began to build a smaller but more profitable empire in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>. Settlement along the South American coast in what is today <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> began in 1624, and a colony was founded on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a> in 1625 (the island had to be shared with the English until the Treaty of Utrecht in 1713, when it was ceded outright). The <i><a href="/wiki/Compagnie_des_%C3%8Eles_de_l%27Am%C3%A9rique" title="Compagnie des &#206;les de l\'Am&#233;rique">Compagnie des &#206;les de l\'Am&#233;rique</a></i> founded colonies in <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> in 1635, and a colony was later founded on <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> by (1650). The food-producing plantations of these colonies were built and sustained through slavery, with the supply of slaves dependent on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_slave_trade" title="African slave trade">African slave trade</a>. Local resistance by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a> resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Carib_Expulsion" title="Carib Expulsion">Carib Expulsion</a> of 1660.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> France\'s most important Caribbean colonial possession was established in 1664, when the colony of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> (today\'s <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>) was founded on the western half of the Spanish island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>. In the 18th century, Saint-Domingue grew to be the richest sugar colony in the Caribbean. The eastern half of Hispaniola (today\'s <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>) also came under French rule for a short period, after being given to France by Spain in 1795.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p><h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa_and_Asia">Africa and Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Africa and Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:French_colonisation_in_Africa" title="Category:French colonisation in Africa">Category:French colonisation in Africa</a>.</div><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7afrique" title="Fran&#231;afrique">Fran&#231;afrique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1343" data-file-width="1713" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg/250px-Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg/375px-Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg/500px-Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arrival_of_Marshal_Randon_in_Algier-Ernest-Francis_Vacherot_mg_5120.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arrival of Marshal <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Louis_Randon" title="Jacques Louis Randon">Randon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> in 1857, by Ernest Francis Vacherot</div></div></div>\n<p>French colonial expansion was not limited to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> in West Africa, the French began to establish trading posts along the coast in 1624. In 1664, the <a href="/wiki/French_East_India_Company" title="French East India Company">French East India Company</a> was established to compete for trade in the east. With the decay of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, in 1830 the French seized <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, thus beginning the colonization of <a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a>.\n</p><p>During the First World War, after France had suffered heavy casualties on the Western Front, they began to recruit soldiers from their African empire. By 1917, France had recruited 270,000 African soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew-20">[20]</a></sup> Their most decorated regiments came from Morocco, but due to the ongoing <a href="/wiki/Zaian_War" title="Zaian War">Zaian War</a> they were only able to recruit 23,000 Moroccans. African soldiers had success in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verdun" title="Battle of Verdun">Battle of Verdun</a> and failure in the <a href="/wiki/Nivelle_Offensive" title="Nivelle Offensive">Nivelle Offensive</a>, but in general regardless of their usefulness, French generals did not think highly of their African troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew-20">[20]</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the First World War, France\'s African war aims were not being decided by her cabinet or the official mind of the colonial ministry, but rather the leaders of the colonial movement in French Africa. The first occasion of this was in 1915&#8211;1916, when Francois Georges-Picot (both a diplomat and part of a colonial dynasty) met with the British to discuss the division of Cameroon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew-20">[20]</a></sup> Picot proceeded with negotiations with neither the oversight of the French president nor the cabinet. What resulted was Britain giving nine tenths of Cameroon to the French. Picot emphasized the demands of the French colonists over the French cabinet. This policy of French colonial leaders determining France\'s African war aims can be seen throughout much of France\'s empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Colonies were established in India\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chandernagore" title="Chandernagore">Chandernagore</a> (1673) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pondicherry_district" title="Pondicherry district">Pondich&#233;ry</a> in the south east (1674), and later at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yanam,_French_India" title="Yanam, French India">Yanam</a> (1723), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mah%C3%A9,_India" title="Mah&#233;, India">Mahe</a> (1725), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karikal" title="Karikal">Karikal</a> (1739) (see <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French India</a>). Colonies were also founded in the Indian Ocean, on the &#206;le de Bourbon (<a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R&#233;union">R&#233;union</a>, 1664), <a href="/wiki/Isle_de_France_(Mauritius)" title="Isle de France (Mauritius)">Isle de France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, 1718), and the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> (1756).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_conflict_with_Britain">Colonial conflict with Britain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial conflict with Britain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Seven_Years%27_War" title="France in the Seven Years\' War">France in the Seven Years\' War</a> and <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="France in the American Revolutionary War">France in the American Revolutionary War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="1140" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png/250px-European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png/375px-European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png/500px-European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_settlements_in_India_1501-1739.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French and other European settlements in <a href="/wiki/Colonial_India" title="Colonial India">Colonial India</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martinique_1809.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="751" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Martinique_1809.jpg/250px-Martinique_1809.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Martinique_1809.jpg/375px-Martinique_1809.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Martinique_1809.jpg/500px-Martinique_1809.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martinique_1809.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Martinique_(1809)" title="Invasion of Martinique (1809)">invasion of Martinique</a> in 1809</div></div></div>\n<p>In the middle of the 18th century, a series of colonial conflicts began between France and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Britain</a>, which ultimately resulted in the destruction of most of the first French colonial empire and the near-complete expulsion of France from the Americas. These wars were the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> (1744&#8211;1748), the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years\' War">Seven Years\' War</a> (1756&#8211;1763), the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> (1765&#8211;1783), the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a> (1793&#8211;1802) and the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> (1803&#8211;1815). It may even be seen further back in time to the first of the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_Wars" title="French and Indian Wars">French and Indian Wars</a>. This cyclic conflict is sometimes known as the <a href="/wiki/Second_Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Second Hundred Years\' War">Second Hundred Years\' War</a>.\n</p><p>Although the War of the Austrian Succession was indecisive &#8211; despite French successes in India under the French Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Fran%C3%A7ois_Dupleix" title="Joseph Fran&#231;ois Dupleix">Joseph Fran&#231;ois Dupleix</a> and Europe under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshal_Saxe" title="Marshal Saxe">Marshal Saxe</a> &#8211; the Seven Years\' War, after early French successes in <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorca</a> and North America, saw a French defeat, with the numerically superior British (over one million to about 50 thousand French settlers) conquering not only <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> (excluding the small islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a>), but also most of France\'s West Indian (Caribbean) colonies, and all of the <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">French Indian outposts</a>.\n</p><p>While the peace treaty saw France\'s Indian outposts, and the Caribbean islands of Martinique and Guadeloupe restored to France, the competition for influence in India had been won by the British, and North America was entirely lost &#8211; most of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> was taken by Britain (also referred to as <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a>), except <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, which France ceded to Spain as payment for Spain\'s late entrance into the war (and as compensation for Britain\'s annexation of Spanish Florida). Also ceded to the British were <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> in the West Indies. Although the loss of Canada would cause much regret in future generations, it excited little unhappiness at the time; colonialism was widely regarded as both unimportant to France, and immoral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some recovery of the French colonial empire was made during the <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_American_Revolutionary_War" title="France in the American Revolutionary War">French intervention in the American Revolution</a>, with Saint Lucia being returned to France by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">Treaty of Paris</a> in 1783, but not nearly as much as had been hoped for at the time of French intervention. True disaster came to what remained of France\'s colonial empire in 1791 when Saint Domingue (the Western third of the Caribbean island of <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>), France\'s richest and most important colony, was riven by a massive slave revolt, caused partly by the divisions among the island\'s elite, which had resulted from the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> of 1789.\n</p><p>The slaves, led eventually by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toussaint_L%27Ouverture" title="Toussaint L\'Ouverture">Toussaint L\'Ouverture</a> and then, following his capture by the French in 1801, by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Jean-Jacques Dessalines</a>, held their own against French and British opponents, and ultimately achieved independence as <a href="/wiki/First_Empire_of_Haiti" title="First Empire of Haiti">Empire of Haiti</a> in 1804 (Haiti became the first black republic in the world, followed by Liberia in 1847).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The black and mulatto population of the island (including the Spanish east) had declined from 700,000 in 1789 to 351,819 in 1804. About 80,000 Haitians died in the 1802&#8211;03 campaign alone. Of the 55,131 French soldiers dispatched to Haiti in 1802&#8211;03, 45,000, including 18 generals, had died, along with 10,000 sailors, the great majority from disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Captain [first name unknown] Sorrell of the British navy observed, "France lost there one of the finest armies she ever sent forth, composed of picked veterans, the conquerors of Italy and of German legions. She is now entirely deprived of her influence and her power in the West Indies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the meanwhile, the newly resumed war with Britain by the French, resulted in the British capture of practically all remaining French colonies. These were restored at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amiens" title="Treaty of Amiens">Treaty of Amiens</a> in 1802, but when war resumed in 1803, the British soon recaptured them. France\'s repurchase of Louisiana in 1800 came to nothing, as the success of the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> convinced Napoleon that holding Louisiana would not be worth the cost, leading to <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">its sale</a> to the United States in 1803. The French attempt to establish a colony in Egypt in 1798&#8211;1801 was not successful. Battle casualties for the campaign were at least 15,000 killed or wounded and 8,500 prisoners for France; 50,000 killed or wounded and 15,000 prisoners for Turkey, Egypt, other Ottoman lands, and Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p><p><span id="Second_French_colonial_empire"></span>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="Second_French_colonial_empire_.28after_1830.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_French_colonial_empire_(after_1830)">Second French colonial empire (after 1830)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Second French colonial empire (after 1830)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_Empire_evolution.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/French_Empire_evolution.gif/280px-French_Empire_evolution.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/French_Empire_evolution.gif/420px-French_Empire_evolution.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/French_Empire_evolution.gif/560px-French_Empire_evolution.gif 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:French_Empire_evolution.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Animated map showing the growth and decline of the first and second French colonial empires</div></div></div>\n<p>At the close of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, most of France\'s colonies were restored to it by Britain, notably <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> on the coast of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, various trading posts in <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, the <i>&#206;le Bourbon</i> (<a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9union" title="R&#233;union">R&#233;union</a>) in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, and France\'s tiny Indian possessions; however, <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">Britain</a> finally annexed <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>, and the <i>Isle de France</i> (now <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>).\n</p><p>In 1825 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_X" title="Charles X">Charles X</a> sent an expedition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ha%C3%AFti" title="Ha&#239;ti">Ha&#239;ti</a>, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Haiti_indemnity_controversy" title="Haiti indemnity controversy">Haiti indemnity controversy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The beginnings of the second French colonial empire were laid in 1830 with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_rule_in_Algeria" title="French rule in Algeria">French invasion of Algeria</a>, which was conquered over the next 17 years. One authority counts 825,000 Algerian victims of the French conquest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Napoleon_III:_1852.E2.80.9370"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoleon_III:_1852&#8211;70">Napoleon III: 1852&#8211;70</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Napoleon III: 1852&#8211;70">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:III._Nap%C3%B3leon_(%C3%B6reg).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="893" data-file-width="593" decoding="async" height="301" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg/200px-III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg/300px-III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg/400px-III._Nap%C3%B3leon_%28%C3%B6reg%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:III._Nap%C3%B3leon_(%C3%B6reg).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The last photograph of Napoleon III (1872)</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a> doubled the area of the French overseas Empire; he established French rule in <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cochinchina" title="Cochinchina">Cochinchina</a>, established a protectorate in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> (1863); and colonized parts of Africa. He joined Britain sending an army to China during <a href="/wiki/Second_Opium_War" title="Second Opium War">Second Opium War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Taiping_Rebellion" title="Taiping Rebellion">Taiping Rebellion</a> (1860), but French ventures to establish influence in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> (1867) and <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a> (1866) were less successful. His attempt to impose a European monarch, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Maximilian I of Mexico</a> on the Mexicans ended in a spectacular failure in 1867. To restore the Mexican Republic, 31,962 Mexicans died violently, including over 11,000 executed by firing squads, 8,304 were seriously wounded and 33,281 endured captivity in prisoner of war camps. Those Mexicans who fought for the monarchy sacrificed 5,671 of their number killed in combat, 2,159 badly wounded, and 4,379 taken prisoner. The French suffered 1,729 battle deaths, including 549 who died of wounds, 2,559 wounded, and 4,925 dead from disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>To carry out his new overseas projects, Napoleon III created a new Ministry of the Navy and the Colonies, and appointed an energetic minister, <a href="/wiki/Prosper_de_Chasseloup-Laubat" title="Prosper de Chasseloup-Laubat">Prosper, Marquis of Chasseloup-Laubat</a>, to head it. A key part of the enterprise was the modernization of the French Navy; he began the construction of fifteen powerful new battle cruisers powered by steam and driven by propellers; and a fleet of steam powered troop transports. The French Navy became the second most powerful in the world, after Britain\'s. He also created a new force of colonial troops, including elite units of naval infantry, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zouaves" title="Zouaves">Zouaves</a>, the Chasseurs d\'Afrique, and Algerian sharpshooters, and he expanded the Foreign Legion, which had been founded in 1831 and won fame in the Crimea, Italy and Mexico. By the end of Napoleon III\'s reign the French overseas territories had tripled in area; in 1870 they covered a million square kilometers, with more than five million inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="New_Caledonia_becomes_a_French_possession_.281853.E2.80.9354.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Caledonia_becomes_a_French_possession_(1853&#8211;54)">New Caledonia becomes a French possession (1853&#8211;54)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: New Caledonia becomes a French possession (1853&#8211;54)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 24 September 1853, Admiral <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Febvrier_Despointes" title="Auguste Febvrier Despointes">Febvrier Despointes</a> took formal possession of <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port-de-France" title="Port-de-France">Port-de-France</a> (Noum&#233;a) was founded 25 June 1854. A few dozen free settlers settled on the west coast in the following years, but New Caledonia became a <a href="/wiki/Penal_colony" title="Penal colony">penal colony</a> and, from the 1860s until the end of the transportations in 1897, about 22,000 criminals and political prisoners were sent to New Caledonia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gb-1_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-gb-1-31">[31]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Colonization_of_Senegal_.281854.E2.80.9365.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonization_of_Senegal_(1854&#8211;65)">Colonization of Senegal (1854&#8211;65)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Colonization of Senegal (1854&#8211;65)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Senegal" title="French Senegal">French Senegal</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1431" data-file-width="1961" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg/250px-Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg/375px-Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg/500px-Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le_prince_de_Joinville_sur_l%27%C3%AEle_de_Gor%C3%A9e_en_1842.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French trading post on <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gor&#233;e">Gor&#233;e</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At the beginning of Napoleon III\'s reign, the presence of France in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Senegal" title="French Senegal">Senegal</a> was limited to a trading post on the island of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goree" title="Goree">Goree</a>, a narrow strip on the coast, the town of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis,_Senegal" title="Saint-Louis, Senegal">Saint-Louis</a>, and a handful of trading posts in the interior. The economy had largely been based on the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">slave trade</a>, carried out by the rulers of the small kingdoms of the interior, until France <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abolition_of_slavery" title="Abolition of slavery">abolished slavery</a> in its colonies in 1848. In 1854, Napoleon III named an enterprising <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French</a> officer, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Faidherbe" title="Louis Faidherbe">Louis Faidherbe</a>, to govern and expand the colony, and to give it the beginning of a modern economy. Faidherbe built a series of forts along the Senegal River, formed alliances with leaders in the interior, and sent expeditions against those who resisted French rule. He built a new port at <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a>, established and protected telegraph lines and roads, followed these with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dakar-Saint-Louis_railway" title="Dakar-Saint-Louis railway">rail line between Dakar and Saint-Louis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dakar%E2%80%93Niger_Railway" title="Dakar&#8211;Niger Railway">another into the interior</a>. He built schools, bridges, and systems to supply fresh water to the towns. He also introduced the large-scale cultivation of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bambara_groundnuts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bambara groundnuts (page does not exist)">Bambara groundnuts</a> and peanuts as a commercial crop. Reaching into the <a href="/wiki/Niger_River" title="Niger River">Niger</a> valley, Senegal became the primary French base in <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">West Africa</a> and a model colony. Dakar became one of the most important cities of the French Empire and of Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Intervention_in_China_.281858.E2.80.9360.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Intervention_in_China_(1858&#8211;60)">Intervention in China (1858&#8211;60)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Intervention in China (1858&#8211;60)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1857, after the murder of a French priest and the arrest by the Chinese police of the crew of a British merchant ship, Napoleon III joined together with Great Britain to form a military expedition to punish the Chinese government. The object of his policy was not to take territory, but to assure that the vast and lucrative Chinese market was open to French commerce, and not the exclusive trading partner of Britain. In January 1858 a combined British and French fleet bombarded and occupied <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Canton</a>, and landed troops at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Hai_River" title="Hai River">Hai River</a> in northern China. In June 1858 the Chinese government in Peking was forced to sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tientsin" title="Treaty of Tientsin">Treaty of Tientsin</a> with Britain, France, Russia and the United States. This treaty opened six additional Chinese ports to European merchant ships, allowed Christian missionary activity, and legalized the import of opium into China.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1872" data-file-width="2641" decoding="async" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg/250px-Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg/375px-Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg/500px-Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Looting_of_the_Yuan_Ming_Yuan_by_Anglo_French_forces_in_1860.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Anglo-French forces pillage China\'s <a href="/wiki/Summer_Palace" title="Summer Palace">Summer Palace</a>, October 1860.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Chinese government was reluctant to observe the treaty, so Napoleon III and the British Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Palmerston" title="Lord Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a> decided to take more forceful action, in what became known in history as the second phase of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Opium_War" title="Second Opium War">Second Opium War</a>. A joint French-British expeditionary force of 8,000 men was created under a French general, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Cousin-Montauban" title="Charles Cousin-Montauban">Charles Cousin-Montauban</a>, who had commanded French forces in Algeria. At the beginning of 1860 the French-British fleet sailed from Europe, and in the spring of 1860 landed the army in China. The Anglo-French army force, led by Cousin-Montauban, captured Tientsin, and then marched on the capital. On 21 September 1860 it defeated the army of the Chinese emperor at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Palikao" title="Battle of Palikao">Battle of Palikao</a> and seized the capital Beijing. At the orders of the British commander <a href="/wiki/James_Bruce,_8th_Earl_of_Elgin" title="James Bruce, 8th Earl of Elgin">Lord Elgin</a>, the British and French forces burned and pillaged the <a href="/wiki/Old_Summer_Palace" title="Old Summer Palace">Old Summer Palace</a> of the Chinese Emperor. On 25 October 1860, the Chinese Emperor was obliged to accept a second treaty of Tientsin, opening an additional eleven new ports to European trade, making westerners immune to prosecution by Chinese courts, and establishing western diplomatic missions in Beijing. Some of the art objects taken from the looted Summer Palace were carried to France, where the Empress used them to decorate a Chinese-themed salon at the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Fontainebleau" title="Palace of Fontainebleau">Palace of Fontainebleau</a>, where they can be seen today.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="France_in_Korea_and_Japan_.281866.E2.80.9368.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="France_in_Korea_and_Japan_(1866&#8211;68)">France in Korea and Japan (1866&#8211;68)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: France in Korea and Japan (1866&#8211;68)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_campaign_against_Korea_(1866)" title="French campaign against Korea (1866)">French campaign against Korea (1866)</a></div>\n<p>In 1866, French diplomats in China learned that French priests had been arrested and executed in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Korea" title="History of Korea">Korea</a>, a country which had had no diplomatic or commercial contact with Europe or America. Twelve Catholic priests at the time were living in Korea, with an estimated 23,000 Korean converts, belonging to churches founded by French missionaries in the 18th century. In January 1866, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gojong_of_the_Korean_Empire" title="Gojong of the Korean Empire">King Gojong</a> and his father, the regent, ordered the execution of most of the French priests, and ten thousand converts. A squadron of French ships, carrying eight hundred naval infantry, attempted retaliation but made little headway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Japan the Meiji Emperor, and his enemies, the <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_shogunate" title="Tokugawa shogunate">Tokugawa shogunate</a>, both sought French military training and technology in their battle for power, known as the <a href="/wiki/Boshin_War" title="Boshin War">Boshin War</a>.\nIn 1867, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_military_mission_to_Japan_(1867%E2%80%931868)" title="French military mission to Japan (1867&#8211;1868)">military mission to Japan</a> played a key role in modernizing the troops of the <i><a href="/wiki/Sh%C5%8Dgun" title="Sh&#333;gun">sh&#333;gun</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Tokugawa_Yoshinobu" title="Tokugawa Yoshinobu">Tokugawa Yoshinobu</a>, and even participated on his side against Imperial troops during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boshin_war" title="Boshin war">Boshin war</a>. The European representative of the Shogunate, <a href="/wiki/Shibata_Takenaka" title="Shibata Takenaka">Shibata Takenaka</a>, approached both Britain and France, asking assistance to build a modern shipyard and to train the Shogunate army in modern western warfare. The shipyard, which became the naval base of <a href="/wiki/Yokosuka" title="Yokosuka">Yokosuka</a>, was designed by the French engineer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonce_Verny" title="Leonce Verny">Leonce Verny</a>. The British, who supported the imperial faction, declined to provide trainers, but Napoleon III agreed, and in 1867 dispatched a delegation of nineteen French military experts in the fields of infantry, cavalry and artillery to Japan. They trained an elite corps, called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Denshutai" title="Denshutai">Denshutai</a>, to fight on the side of the <i>sh&#333;gun</i>.\n</p><p>On the other side, the Emperor purchased from the United States a French-built ironclad warship, renamed the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_ironclad_K%C5%8Dtetsu" title="Japanese ironclad K&#333;tetsu">Kotetsu</a> (literally "ironclad"). It played an important role in the first modern naval battle fought in Japan. By 1868, the Imperial forces had won a decisive victory. French influence in the Japanese navy remained strong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="France_in_Indochina_and_the_Pacific_.281858.E2.80.9370.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="France_in_Indochina_and_the_Pacific_(1858&#8211;70)">France in Indochina and the Pacific (1858&#8211;70)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: France in Indochina and the Pacific (1858&#8211;70)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="705" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg/220px-Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg/330px-Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg/440px-Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parade_of_the_Kanaks_districts_before_Queen_Pomare_in_1860.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queen <a href="/wiki/P%C5%8Dmare_IV" title="P&#333;mare IV">P&#333;mare IV</a> in 1860. <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tahiti" title="Kingdom of Tahiti">Tahiti</a> was made a French protectorate in 1842, and annexed as a colony of France in 1880.</div></div></div>\n<p>Napoleon III also acted to increase the French presence in Indochina. An important factor in his decision was the belief that France risked becoming a second-rate power by not expanding its influence in East Asia. Deeper down was the sense that France owed the world a civilizing mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>French missionaries had been active in Vietnam since the 17th century, when the Jesuit priest <a href="/wiki/Alexandre_de_Rhodes" title="Alexandre de Rhodes">Alexandre de Rhodes</a> opened a mission there. In 1858 the Vietnamese emperor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nguyen_Dynasty" title="Nguyen Dynasty">Nguyen Dynasty</a> felt threatened by the French influence and tried to expel the missionaries. Napoleon III sent a naval force of fourteen gunships, carrying three thousand French and three thousand Filipino troops provided by Spain, under <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rigault_de_Genouilly" title="Charles Rigault de Genouilly">Charles Rigault de Genouilly</a>, to compel the government to accept the missionaries and to stop the persecution of Catholics. In September 1858 the expeditionary force captured and occupied the port of <a href="/wiki/Da_Nang" title="Da Nang">Da Nang</a>, and then in February 1859 moved south and captured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saigon" title="Saigon">Saigon</a>. The Vietnamese ruler was compelled to cede three provinces to France, and to offer protection to the Catholics. The French troops departed for a time to take part in the expedition to China, but in 1862, when the agreements were not fully followed by the Vietnamese emperor, they returned. The Emperor was forced to open treaty ports in <a href="/wiki/Annam_(French_protectorate)" title="Annam (French protectorate)">Annam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tonkin" title="Tonkin">Tonkin</a>, and all of <a href="/wiki/Cochinchina" title="Cochinchina">Cochinchina</a> became a French territory in 1864.\n</p><p>In 1863, the ruler of <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>, King <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norodom" title="Norodom">Norodom</a>, who had been placed in power by the government of <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, rebelled against his sponsors and sought the protection of France. The Thai Emperor granted authority over Cambodia to France, in exchange for two provinces of <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a>, which were ceded by Cambodia to Thailand. In 1867, Cambodia formally became a protectorate of France.\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:41px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="654" data-file-width="1148" decoding="async" height="68" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg/120px-Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg/180px-Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg/240px-Prise_de_Saigon_18_Fevrier_1859_Antoine_Morel-Fatio.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saigon" title="Siege of Saigon">Capture of Saigon</a> by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rigault_de_Genouilly" title="Charles Rigault de Genouilly">Charles Rigault de Genouilly</a> on 18 February 1859, painted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antoine_Morel-Fatio" title="Antoine Morel-Fatio">Antoine Morel-Fatio</a>\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:45.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="984" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="59" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG/120px-Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG/180px-Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG/240px-Jean-Leon_Gerome_001.JPG 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>Napoleon III receiving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/France-Thailand_relations" title="France-Thailand relations">Siamese embassy</a> at the palace of Fontainebleau in 1864\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="Intervention_in_Syria_and_Lebanon_.281860.E2.80.9361.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Intervention_in_Syria_and_Lebanon_(1860&#8211;61)">Intervention in Syria and Lebanon (1860&#8211;61)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Intervention in Syria and Lebanon (1860&#8211;61)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1538" data-file-width="2973" decoding="async" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg/220px-French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg/330px-French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg/440px-French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:French_expeditionary_corps_landing_in_Beyrouth_16_August_1860.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/R%C3%A8glement_Organique_(Mount_Lebanon)" title="R&#232;glement Organique (Mount Lebanon)">French expedition in Syria</a> led by General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beaufort_d%27Hautpoul" title="Beaufort d\'Hautpoul">Beaufort d\'Hautpoul</a>, landing in Beyrouth on 16 August 1860</div></div></div>\n<p>In the spring of 1860, a war broke out in <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, then part of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, between the quasi-Muslim <a href="/wiki/Druze" title="Druze">Druze</a> population and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maronite_Christians" title="Maronite Christians">Maronite Christians</a>. The Ottoman authorities in Lebanon could not stop the violence, and it spread into neighboring <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, with the massacre of many Christians. In <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>, the Emir Abd-el-Kadr protected the Christians there against the Muslim rioters. Napoleon III felt obliged to intervene on behalf of the Christians, despite the opposition of London, which feared it would lead to a wider French presence in the Middle East. After long and difficult negotiations to obtain the approval of the British government, Napoleon III sent a French contingent of seven thousand men for a period of six months. The troops arrived in Beirut in August 1860, and took positions in the mountains between the Christian and Muslim communities. Napoleon III organized an international conference in Paris, where the country was placed under the rule of a Christian governor named by the Ottoman Sultan, which restored a fragile peace. The French troops departed in June 1861, after just under one year. The French intervention alarmed the British, but was highly popular with the powerful Catholic political faction in France, which had been alarmed by Napoleon\'s dispute with the Pope over his territories in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Algeria">Algeria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Algeria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="662" data-file-width="702" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/220px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/330px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/440px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French conquest of Algeria</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Algeria had been formally under French rule since 1830, but only in 1852 was the country entirely conquered. There were about a hundred thousand European settlers in the country, at that time, about half of them French. Under the Second Republic the country was ruled by a civilian government, but Louis Napoleon re-established a military government, much to the annoyance of the colonists. By 1857 the army had conquered Kabyle Province, and pacified the country. By 1860 the European population had grown to two hundred thousand, and the land of the Algerians was being rapidly bought and farmed by the new arrivals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 500,000 and 1,000,000, from approximately 3 million Algerians, were killed within the first three decades of the conquest as a result of war, massacres, disease and famine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kiernan2007_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kiernan2007-40">[40]</a></sup> French losses from 1830&#8211;51 were 3,336 killed in action and 92,329 dead in the hospital.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the first eight years of his rule Napoleon III paid little attention to Algeria. In September 1860, however, he and the Empress Eug&#233;nie visited Algeria, and the trip made a deep impression upon them. Eug&#233;nie was invited to attend a traditional Arab wedding, and the Emperor met many of the local leaders. The Emperor gradually conceived the idea that Algeria should be governed differently from other colonies. in February 1863, he wrote a public letter to Pelissier, the Military Governor, saying: "Algeria is not a colony in the traditional sense, but an Arab kingdom; the local people have, like the colonists, a legal right to my protection. I am just as much the Emperor of the Arabs of Algeria as I am of the French." He intended to rule Algeria through a government of Arab aristocrats. Toward this end he invited the chiefs of main Algerian tribal groups to his chateau at Compiegne for hunting and festivities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Compared to previous administrations, Napoleon III was far more sympathetic to the native Algerians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> He halted European migration inland, restricting them to the coastal zone. He also freed the Algerian rebel leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abd_al-Qadir_al-Jaza%27iri" title="Abd al-Qadir al-Jaza\'iri">Abd al Qadir</a> (who had been promised freedom on surrender but was imprisoned by the previous administration) and gave him a stipend of 150,000 francs. He allowed Muslims to serve in the military and civil service on theoretically equal terms and allowed them to migrate to France. In addition, he gave the option of citizenship; however, for Muslims to take this option they had to accept all of the French civil code, including parts governing inheritance and marriage which conflicted with Muslim laws, and they had to reject the competence of religious <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharia</a> courts. This was interpreted by some Muslims as requiring them to give up parts of their religion to obtain citizenship and was resented.\n</p><p>More importantly, Napoleon III changed the system of land tenure. While ostensibly well-intentioned, in effect this move destroyed the traditional system of land management and deprived many Algerians of land. While Napoleon did renounce state claims to tribal lands, he also began a process of dismantling tribal land ownership in favour of individual land ownership. This process was corrupted by French officials sympathetic to the French in Algeria who took much of the land they surveyed into public domain. In addition, many tribal leaders, chosen for loyalty to the French rather than influence in their tribe, immediately sold communal land for cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>\n</p><p>His attempted reforms were interrupted in 1864 by an Arab insurrection, which required more than a year and an army of 85,000 soldiers to suppress. Nonetheless, he did not give up his idea of making Algeria a model where French colonists and Arabs could live and work together as equals. He traveled to Algiers for a second time on 3 May 1865, and this time he remained for a month, meeting with tribal leaders and local officials. He offered a wide amnesty to participants of the insurrection, and promised to name Arabs to high positions in his government. He also promised a large public works program of new ports, railroads, and roads. However, once again his plans met a major natural obstacle\' in 1866 and 1867, Algeria was struck by an epidemic of cholera, clouds of locusts, draught and famine, and his reforms were hindered by the French colonists, who voted massively against him in the plebiscites of his late reign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="French_intervention_in_Mexico_.281862.E2.80.9367.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_intervention_in_Mexico_(1862&#8211;67)">French intervention in Mexico (1862&#8211;67)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: French intervention in Mexico (1862&#8211;67)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_intervention_in_Mexico" title="French intervention in Mexico">French intervention in Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Mexican_Empire" title="Second Mexican Empire">Second Mexican Empire</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2565" data-file-width="1885" decoding="async" height="299" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg/220px-Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg/330px-Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg/440px-Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emperador_Maximiliano_I_de_Mexico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Napoleon III tried unsuccessfully to place <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Maximilian I</a>, brother of the Austrian Emperor, on the throne of Mexico. Portrait by <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Winterhalter" title="Franz Xaver Winterhalter">Franz Xaver Winterhalter</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Castle" title="Chapultepec Castle">Chapultepec Castle</a>, Mexico.</div></div></div>\n<p>In December 1862, the conservative Mexican government was overthrown by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benito_Juarez" title="Benito Juarez">Benito Juarez</a>, who established a secular state and refused to pay the internal and external debts of the old government.
