France was the largest owner of the debt, owed 135 million gold francs of the 260 million francs total. The rest of the debt was owed to Britain (85 million francs) and Spain (40 million). Under an 1861 agreement, France, Britain and Spain organized a joint military force to compel the Mexican government to pay. A British-French flotilla of ships arrived at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">VeraCruz</a> in December 1861 and landed 7500 French soldiers and 700 British soldiers, joined later by 6000 Spanish soldiers from <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>.\n</p><p>Juarez opened negotiations with the international force, but it soon became evident that the French expedition had a more ambitious objective than debt repayment. Napoleon III and the Empress had been intensively lobbied by Mexican &#233;migr&#233;s in Europe, who proposed that France establish a new conservative and Catholic government in Mexico, under a European monarch. Napoleon III was told that the new monarch would be welcomed by the entire Mexican population. He consented to launch the operation if the new monarch would be approved by a national plebiscite, as he had been. The monarch selected for this task was <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">the Archduke Maximilian</a>, the brother of the Austrian Emperor Franz-Joseph II, and husband of <a href="/wiki/Carlota_of_Mexico" title="Carlota of Mexico">Carlota of Mexico</a>, daughter of the King of Belgium.\n</p><p>When the British and Spanish realized the French goals, they withdrew from the expedition, but the French marched on Mexico City. The first attempt by General Lorencez was repulsed by the forces of General <a href="/wiki/Ignacio_Zaragoza" title="Ignacio Zaragoza">Ignacio Zaragoza</a> at <a href="/wiki/Puebla" title="Puebla">Puebla</a> on 5 May 1862, the first defeat of a French Army since Waterloo. Napoleon III appointed a new commander, General Forey, one of the victors of Solferino, and sent 23,000 fresh soldiers. Napoleon III believed that the Mexican people would embrace the new government. He also knew that the government of the United States would be unable to prevent it, even though it was in contravention of the <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">Monroe Doctrine</a>, because of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> then underway, and the implicit support provided by the neighboring Confederate States of America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The reinforced French army under Forey launched a new offensive from March to June 1863. After bitter resistance, the defenders of Mexico City surrendered on 7 June 1863. Forey, disregarding Napoleon III\'s instructions not to install a monarch without a popular plebiscite, organized an assembly of Mexican notables who proclaimed the Mexican Empire and invited <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Maximilian I of Mexico</a> to rule. Ruling President <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez" title="Benito Ju&#225;rez">Benito Ju&#225;rez</a> and his Republican forces retreated to the countryside and fought against the French troops and the Mexican monarchists.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="582" decoding="async" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg/220px-San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg/330px-San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg/440px-San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Pablo_del_Monte.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French <a href="/wiki/Chasseurs_d%27Afrique" title="Chasseurs d\'Afrique">chasseurs d\'Afrique</a> taking the standard of the Durango lancers at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_San_Pablo_del_Monte" title="Battle of San Pablo del Monte">Battle of San Pablo del Monte</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Maximilian was a reluctant Emperor, not arriving in Mexico until June 1864. One of his first acts was to sign an agreement that Mexico would repay France the entire cost of the war. The combined Mexican monarchist and French forces won victories up until 1865, but then the tide began to turn against them, in part because the American Civil War had ended. The U.S. government demanded that France withdraw its soldiers from Mexico. Facing a guerilla war and a financial catastrophe, the Emperor Maximilian became more and more depressed, leaving the capital for long periods and allowing the <a href="/wiki/Carlota_of_Mexico" title="Carlota of Mexico">Empress Carlota</a> to reign. Not willing to have a war with the United States, Napoleon III decided at the beginning of 1866 to withdraw French troops from Mexico. In 1863 Maximilian had sent Carlota to Europe to appeal for funds and support. She appealed to Napoleon III, but he refused to provide more troops or money. During her tour of European courts, she lost and never regained her sanity. Maximilian refused pleas that he depart, and fought against the growing partisan army of Juarez. He was captured, judged, and shot on 19 June 1867.\n</p><p>The misadventure in Mexico cost the lives of six thousand French soldiers and 336 million francs, in a campaign originally designed to collect 60 million francs. It also aroused the hostility of both the United States and Austria, which had lost a member of its royal family. It was also a distraction to Napoleon III, on the eve of his coming confrontation with Prussia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:41.5px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG"><img alt="" data-file-height="772" data-file-width="1383" decoding="async" height="67" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG/120px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG/180px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG/240px-Si%C3%A8ge_de_Puebla_-_29_mars_1863.PNG 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p><a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Puebla_(1863)" title="Siege of Puebla (1863)">Siege of Puebla</a>, Mexico by the French Army\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">\n<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:24px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edouard_Manet_022.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1714" data-file-width="2024" decoding="async" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Edouard_Manet_022.jpg/120px-Edouard_Manet_022.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Edouard_Manet_022.jpg/180px-Edouard_Manet_022.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Edouard_Manet_022.jpg/240px-Edouard_Manet_022.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a></div></div>\n<div class="gallerytext">\n<p>The execution of Maximilian I on 19 June 1867, as painted by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89douard_Manet" title="&#201;douard Manet">&#201;douard Manet</a>. The intervention in Mexico was a disaster for French foreign policy.\n</p>\n</div>\n</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h3><span id="French.E2.80.93British_relations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French&#8211;British_relations">French&#8211;British relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: French&#8211;British relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Despite the signing of the 1860 <a href="/wiki/Cobden%E2%80%93Chevalier_Treaty" title="Cobden&#8211;Chevalier Treaty">Cobden&#8211;Chevalier Treaty</a>, a historic free trade agreement between Britain and France, and the joint operations conducted by France and Britain in the Crimea, China and Mexico, diplomatic relations between Britain and France never became close. <a href="/wiki/Henry_John_Temple,_3rd_Viscount_Palmerston" title="Henry John Temple, 3rd Viscount Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a>, the British foreign minister from 1846 to 1851 and <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">prime minister</a> from 1855 to 1865, sought to maintain the balance of power in Europe; this rarely involved an alignment with France. In 1859 there were even briefly fears that France might try to invade Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Palmerston was suspicious of France\'s interventions in Lebanon, Southeast Asia and Mexico. Palmerston was also concerned that France might intervene in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (1861&#8211;65) on the side of the South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The British also felt threatened by the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> (1859&#8211;1869) by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_de_Lesseps" title="Ferdinand de Lesseps">Ferdinand de Lesseps</a> in Egypt. They tried to oppose its completion by diplomatic pressures and by promoting revolts among workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Suez Canal was successfully built by the French, but became a joint British-French project in 1875. Both nations saw it as vital to maintaining their influence and empires in Asia. In 1882, ongoing civil disturbances in Egypt prompted Britain to intervene, extending a hand to France. France\'s leading expansionist <a href="/wiki/Jules_Ferry" title="Jules Ferry">Jules Ferry</a> was out of office, and Paris allowed London to take effective control of Egypt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="French.E2.80.93U.S._relations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French&#8211;U.S._relations">French&#8211;U.S. relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: French&#8211;U.S. relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/France_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="France in the American Civil War">France in the American Civil War</a></div>\n<p>During 1861 to 1862, at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, Napoleon III considered recognizing the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> in order to protect his operations in Mexico. Washington repeatedly warned that this meant war but the emperor kept this option open, hoping to get Britain as an ally. The Union blockade of southern ports stopped the supply of cotton to textile mills in France, and caused unemployment. The Confederacy had put their faith in <a href="/wiki/Cotton_diplomacy" title="Cotton diplomacy">"King Cotton" diplomacy</a>, expecting that the cutoff of cotton supplies would cause Britain and France to declare war to reopen the trade. Through 1862, Napoleon III met unofficially with Confederate diplomats, raising their hopes that he would unilaterally recognize the Confederacy. France was too weak to act without collaboration with the British, who after much wavering finally rejected intervention as not worth the heavy risk of losing American food exports. Napoleon realized that a war with the U.S. without allies "would spell disaster" for France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In 1863 the Confederacy realized there was no longer any chance of intervention, and expelled the French and British consuls, who were advising their citizens not to enlist in the Confederate Army. In 1865, the United States stationed a large combat Army near the Mexican border as a warning sign. Napoleon III pulled the French troops out, and the "emperor" he had imposed on Mexico was captured and shot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span id="1870.E2.80.931939"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1870&#8211;1939">1870&#8211;1939</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1870&#8211;1939">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Most Frenchmen ignored foreign affairs and colonial issues. In 1914 the chief pressure group was the <i>Parti colonial</i>, a coalition of 50 organizations with a combined total of only 5000 members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg/300px-Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg/450px-Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg/600px-Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presidential_Palace_of_Vietnam.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Hanoi" title="Presidential Palace, Hanoi">Presidential Palace of Vietnam</a>, in Hanoi, was built between 1900 and 1906 to house the French Governor-General of Indochina.</div></div></div>\n<p>It was only after its defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> of 1870&#8211;1871 and the founding of the <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">Third Republic</a> (1871&#8211;1940) that most of France\'s later colonial possessions were acquired. From their base in Cochinchina, the French took over <a href="/wiki/Tonkin" title="Tonkin">Tonkin</a> (in modern <a href="/wiki/Northern_Vietnam" title="Northern Vietnam">northern Vietnam</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Annam_(French_protectorate)" title="Annam (French protectorate)">Annam</a> (in modern <a href="/wiki/Central_Vietnam" title="Central Vietnam">central Vietnam</a>) in 1884&#8211;1885. These, together with Cambodia and Cochinchina, formed <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a> in 1887 (to which <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> was <a href="/wiki/Franco-Siamese_War" title="Franco-Siamese War">added in 1893</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guangzhouwan" title="Guangzhouwan">Guangzhouwan</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> in 1900). In 1849, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_French_Concession" title="Shanghai French Concession">French concession</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a> was established, lasting until 1946.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The French also had <a href="/wiki/Concession_(territory)" title="Concession (territory)">concessions</a> in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hankou" title="Hankou">Hankou</a> (now part of <a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2258" data-file-width="1464" decoding="async" height="432" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg/280px-Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg/420px-Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg/560px-Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonies_of_the_second_French_colonial_empire.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French colonies in 1891 (from <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde_illustr%C3%A9" title="Le Monde illustr&#233;">Le Monde illustr&#233;</a></i>).<br/> 1. Panorama of <i>Lac-Ka&#239;</i>, French outpost in China.<br/> 2. <i>Yun-nan</i>, in the quay of <a href="/wiki/Hanoi" title="Hanoi">Hanoi</a>.<br/> 3. Flooded street of Hanoi.<br/> 4. Landing stage of Hanoi</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>France also extended its influence in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> after 1870, establishing a protectorate in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> in 1881 with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bardo_Treaty" title="Bardo Treaty">Bardo Treaty</a>. Gradually, French control crystallised over much of North, <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a> by around the start of the 20th century (including the modern states of <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, the <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">east African</a> coastal enclave of <a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_Somaliland" title="French Somaliland">French Somaliland</a>), and the island of <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Savorgnan_de_Brazza" title="Pierre Savorgnan de Brazza">Pierre Savorgnan de Brazza</a> helped to formalise French control in Gabon and on the northern banks of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a> from the early 1880s. The explorer Colonel <a href="/wiki/Parfait-Louis_Monteil" title="Parfait-Louis Monteil">Parfait-Louis Monteil</a> traveled from Senegal to <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a> in 1890&#8211;1892, signing treaties of friendship and protection with the rulers of several of the countries he passed through, and gaining much knowledge of the geography and politics of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hirshfield_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hirshfield-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Voulet%E2%80%93Chanoine_Mission" title="Voulet&#8211;Chanoine Mission">Voulet&#8211;Chanoine Mission</a>, a military expedition, set out from Senegal in 1898 to conquer the <a href="/wiki/Chad_Basin" title="Chad Basin">Chad Basin</a> and to unify <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">all French territories in West Africa</a>. This expedition operated jointly with two other expeditions, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foureau-Lamy_Mission" title="Foureau-Lamy Mission">Foureau-Lamy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gentil_Mission" title="Gentil Mission">Gentil Missions</a>, which advanced from <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Congo" title="Middle Congo">Middle Congo</a> respectively. With the death (April 1900) of the Muslim warlord <a href="/wiki/Rabih_az-Zubayr" title="Rabih az-Zubayr">Rabih az-Zubayr</a>, the greatest ruler in the region, and the creation of the Military Territory of Chad (September 1900), the Voulet-Chanoine Mission had accomplished all its goals. The ruthlessness of the mission provoked a scandal in Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2740" data-file-width="3384" decoding="async" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg/350px-Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg/525px-Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg/700px-Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fashoda_Incident_map_-_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Central and east Africa, 1898, during the <a href="/wiki/Fashoda_Incident" title="Fashoda Incident">Fashoda Incident</a></div></div></div>\n<p>As a part of the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>, France aimed to establish a continuous west-east axis across the continent, in contrast with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_to_Cairo_Red_Line" title="Cape to Cairo Red Line">the proposed British north-south axis</a>. Tensions between Britain and France heightened in Africa. At several points war seemed possible, but no outbreak occurred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> The most serious episode was the <a href="/wiki/Fashoda_Incident" title="Fashoda Incident">Fashoda Incident</a> of 1898. French troops tried to claim an area in the Southern Sudan, and a British force purporting to act in the interests of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khedive_of_Egypt" title="Khedive of Egypt">Khedive of Egypt</a> arrived to confront them. Under heavy pressure the French withdrew, implicitly acknowledging Anglo-Egyptian control over the area. An agreement between the two states recognised the <i>status quo</i>: acknowledging British control over Egypt while France became the dominant power in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, but France suffered a humiliating defeat overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Agadir_Crisis" title="Agadir Crisis">Agadir Crisis</a> in 1911 Britain supported France against <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> became a French protectorate.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pacific_islands">Pacific islands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Pacific islands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At this time, the French also established colonies in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Pacific_Ocean" title="South Pacific Ocean">South Pacific</a>, including <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, the various island groups which make up <a href="/wiki/French_Polynesia" title="French Polynesia">French Polynesia</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Society_Islands" title="Society Islands">Society Islands</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marquesas" title="Marquesas">Marquesas</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Tuamotus" title="Tuamotus">Tuamotus</a>), and established joint control of the <a href="/wiki/New_Hebrides" title="New Hebrides">New Hebrides</a> with Britain.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>The French made their last major colonial gains after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, when they gained mandates over the former territories of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> that make up what is now <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, as well as most of the former German colonies of <a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civilising_mission">Civilising mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Civilising mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A hallmark of the French colonial project in the late 19th century and early 20th century was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civilising_mission" title="Civilising mission">civilising mission</a> (<i>mission civilisatrice</i>), the principle that it was Europe\'s duty to bring civilisation to benighted peoples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> As such, colonial officials undertook a policy of Franco-Europeanisation in French colonies, most notably <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">French West Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Madagascar" title="French Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. During the 19th century, French citizenship along with the right to elect a deputy to the French Chamber of Deputies was granted to the four old colonies of Guadeloupe, Martinique, Guyanne and R&#233;union as well as to the residents of the "<a href="/wiki/Four_Communes" title="Four Communes">Four Communes</a>" in Senegal. In most cases, the elected deputies were white Frenchmen, although there were some blacks, such as the Senegalese <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Diagne" title="Blaise Diagne">Blaise Diagne</a>, who was elected in 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segalla_2009_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Segalla_2009-67">[67]</a></sup> Elsewhere, in the largest and most populous colonies, a strict separation between "sujets fran&#231;ais" (all the natives) and "citoyens fran&#231;ais" (all males of European extraction) with different rights and duties was maintained until 1946. As was pointed out in a 1927 treatise on French colonial law, the granting of French citizenship to natives "was not a right, but rather a privilege".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Two 1912 decrees dealing with French West Africa and French Equatorial Africa enumerated the conditions that a native had to meet in order to be granted French citizenship (they included speaking and writing French, earning a decent living and displaying good moral standards). From 1830 to 1946, only between 3,000 and 6,000 native Algerians were granted French citizenship. In French West Africa, outside of the Four Communes, there were 2,500 "citoyens indig&#232;nes" out of a total population of 15 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal,_21may1892.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="923" decoding="async" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg/220px-Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg/330px-Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg/440px-Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal%2C_21may1892.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Desembarco_en_Cotonou_de_tropas_senegalesas._Le_Petit_Journal,_21may1892.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French colonial troops, led by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Alfred-Am%C3%A9d%C3%A9e_Dodds" title="Alfred-Am&#233;d&#233;e Dodds">Alfred-Am&#233;d&#233;e Dodds</a>, a Senegalese mulatto, conquered and annexed <a href="/wiki/Second_Franco-Dahomean_War" title="Second Franco-Dahomean War">Dahomey</a> in 1894</div></div></div>\n<p>French conservatives had been denouncing the assimilationist policies as products of a dangerous liberal fantasy. In the Protectorate of Morocco, the French administration attempted to use urban planning and colonial education to prevent cultural mixing and to uphold the traditional society upon which the French depended for collaboration, with mixed results. After World War II, the segregationist approach modeled in Morocco had been discredited by its connections to Vichyism, and assimilationism enjoyed a brief renaissance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Segalla_2009_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Segalla_2009-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1905, the French abolished <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_slave_trade" title="African slave trade">slavery</a> in most of French West Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> David P. Forsythe wrote: "From Senegal and Mauritania in the west to Niger in the east (what became French Africa), there was a parallel series of ruinous wars, resulting in tremendous numbers of people being violently enslaved. At the beginning of the twentieth century there may have been between 3 and 3.5 million slaves, representing over 30 percent of the total population, within this sparsely populated region."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Critics of French colonialism gained an international audience in the 1920s, and often used documentary reportage and access to agencies such as the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> to make their protests heard. The main criticism was the high level of violence and suffering among the natives. Major critics included <a href="/wiki/Albert_Londres" title="Albert Londres">Albert Londres</a>, F&#233;licien Challaye, and Paul Monet, whose books and articles were widely read.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the first stages of a takeover often involved the destruction of historic buildings in order to use the site for French headquarters, archaeologists and art historians soon engaged in systematic effort to identify, map and preserve historic sites, especially temples such as Angkor Wat, Champa ruins and the temples of Luang Prabang.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Many French museums have collections of colonial materials. Since the 1980s the French government has opened new museums of colonial artifacts including the Mus&#233;e du Quai Branly and the Cit&#233; Nationale de l&#8217;Histoire de l&#8217;Immigration, in Paris; the Centre Culturel Tjibaou in New Caledonia; and the Maison des Civilisations et de l&#8217;Unit&#233; R&#233;unionnaise in R&#233;union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Revolt_in_North_Africa_Against_Spain_and_France">Revolt in North Africa Against Spain and France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Revolt in North Africa Against Spain and France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rif_War" title="Rif War">Rif War</a></div>\n<p>The Berber independence leader <a href="/wiki/Abd_el-Krim" title="Abd el-Krim">Abd el-Krim</a> (1882&#8211;1963) organized armed resistance against the Spanish and French for control of Morocco. The Spanish had faced unrest off and on from the 1890s, but in 1921 Spanish forces were massacred at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Annual" title="Battle of Annual">Battle of Annual</a> El-Krim founded an independent <a href="/wiki/Rif_Republic" title="Rif Republic">Rif Republic</a>  that operated until 1926 but had no international recognition. Paris and Madrid agreed to collaborate to destroy it. They sent in 200,000 soldiers, forcing el-Krim to surrender in 1926; he was exiled in the Pacific until 1947.  Morocco became quiet, and in 1936 became the base from which <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> launched his revolt against Madrid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div aria-labelledby="Free_French_campaigns" class="navbox" role="navigation" hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><b>1940</b>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Mers-el-K%C3%A9bir" title="Attack on Mers-el-K&#233;bir">Mers-el-K&#233;bir</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II#Vichy_French_attacks:_1940" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">Gibraltar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dakar" title="Battle of Dakar">Dakar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gabon" title="Battle of Gabon">Gabon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_French_Indochina" title="Japanese invasion of French Indochina">Indochina</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Franco-Thai_War" title="Franco-Thai War">Franco-Thai War</a> (<a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ko_Chang" title="Battle of Ko Chang">Ko Chang</a>)</li></ul>\n<p><b>1941</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syria-Lebanon_campaign" title="Syria-Lebanon campaign">Syria&#8211;Lebanon</a></li></ul>\n<p><b>1942</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Madagascar" title="Battle of Madagascar">Madagascar</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch"><i>Torch</i></a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Case_Anton" title="Case Anton"><i>Anton</i></a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scuttling_of_the_French_fleet_in_Toulon" title="Scuttling of the French fleet in Toulon">Toulon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_R%C3%A9union" title="Battle of R&#233;union">R&#233;union</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, allied <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free France</a>, often with British support, and Axis-aligned <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a> struggled for control of the colonies, sometimes with outright military combat. By 1943, all of the colonies, except for Indochina under Japanese control, had joined the Free French cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The overseas empire helped liberate France as 300,000 North African Arabs fought in the ranks of the Free French.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> However <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> had no intention of liberating the colonies. He assembled the conference of colonial governors (excluding the nationalist leaders) in Brazzaville in January 1944 to announce plans for postwar Union that would replace the Empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The Brazzaville manifesto proclaimed:\n</p>\n<dl><dd>the goals of the work of civilization undertaken by France in the colonies exclude all idea of autonomy, all possibility of development outside the French block of the Empire; the possible constitutional self-government in the colonies is to be dismissed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p>The manifesto angered nationalists across the Empire, and set the stage for long-term wars in Indochina and Algeria that France would lose in humiliating fashion.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization">Decolonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Decolonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="549" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg/220px-Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg/330px-Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg/440px-Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Militaire_fran%C3%A7ais_surveillant_des_Alg%C3%A9riens.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>French soldiers with suspected Algerian rebels</div></div></div>\n<p>The French colonial empire began to fall during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, when various parts were occupied by foreign powers (Japan in Indochina, Britain in <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Lebanon, and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, the United States and Britain in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, and Germany and Italy in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>). However, control was gradually reestablished by <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>. The <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a>, included in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Constitution_of_1946" title="French Constitution of 1946">Constitution of 1946</a>, nominally replaced the former colonial empire, but officials in Paris remained in full control. The colonies were given local assemblies with only limited local power and budgets. There emerged a group of elites, known as evolu&#233;s, who were natives of the overseas territories but lived in metropolitan France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conflict">Conflict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Conflict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>France was immediately confronted with the beginnings of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a> movement. In Algeria demonstrations in May 1945 were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Setif_and_Guelma_massacre" title="Setif and Guelma massacre">repressed</a> with an estimated 6,000 Algerians killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Unrest in Haiphong, Indochina, in November 1945 was met by another warship bombarding the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ramadier" title="Paul Ramadier">Paul Ramadier</a>\'s (<a href="/wiki/French_Section_of_the_Workers%27_International" title="French Section of the Workers\' International">SFIO</a>) cabinet repressed the <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_Uprising" title="Malagasy Uprising">Malagasy Uprising</a> in Madagascar in 1947. French officials estimated the number of Malagasy killed from a low of 11,000 to a French Army estimate of 89,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Asia, <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietminh" title="Vietminh">Vietminh</a> declared <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>\'s independence, starting the <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">First Indochina War</a>. The French Union\'s struggle against the independence movement, which was backed by the Soviet Union and China.  The war dragged on until 1954 after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dien_Bien_Phu" title="Battle of Dien Bien Phu">Battle of Dien Bien Phu</a> in northern Vietnam and became the last major battle between the French and the Vietnamese in the First Indochina War.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="787" data-file-width="1180" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg/220px-Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg/330px-Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg/440px-Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dien_Bien_Phu_1954_French_prisoners.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Captured French soldiers from Dien Bien Phu, escorted by Vietnamese troops, walk to a prisoner-of-war camp</div></div></div>\n<p>Following the Vietnamese victory Dien Bien Phu and the signing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geneva_Conference_(1954)" title="Geneva Conference (1954)">1954 Geneva Accords</a>. France agreed to withdraw its forces from all its colonies in <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>, while stipulating that Vietnam would be temporarily divided at the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Demilitarized_Zone" title="Vietnamese Demilitarized Zone">17th parallel</a>, with control of the north given to the Viet Minh as the <a href="/wiki/North_Vietnam" title="North Vietnam">Democratic Republic of Vietnam</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">Ho Chi Minh</a>, and the south becoming the <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">State of Vietnam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The refusal of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ng%C3%B4_%C4%90%C3%ACnh_Di%E1%BB%87m" title="Ng&#244; &#272;&#236;nh Di&#7879;m">Ng&#244; &#272;&#236;nh Di&#7879;m</a> (the US-supported president of the first Republic of Vietnam [RVN]) to allow elections in 1956, as had been stipulated by the Geneva Conference, eventually led to the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>.\n</p><p>In France\'s African colonies, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroun" title="Cameroun">Cameroun</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">Union of the Peoples of Cameroon</a>\'s insurrection, started in 1955 and headed by <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Um_Nyob%C3%A9" title="Ruben Um Nyob&#233;">Ruben Um Nyob&#233;</a>, was violently repressed over a two-year period, with perhaps as many as 100 people killed.\n</p><p>French involvement in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> stretched back a century. <a href="/wiki/Ferhat_Abbas" title="Ferhat Abbas">Ferhat Abbas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Messali_Hadj" title="Messali Hadj">Messali Hadj</a>\'s movements had marked the period between the two wars, but both sides radicalised after the Second World War. In 1945, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif_massacre" title="S&#233;tif massacre">S&#233;tif massacre</a> was carried out by the French army.  The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_War_of_Independence" title="Algerian War of Independence">Algerian War</a> started in 1954. <a href="/wiki/Torture_during_the_Algerian_War_of_Independence" title="Torture during the Algerian War of Independence">Atrocities characterized both sides</a>, and the number killed became highly controversial estimates that were made for propaganda purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>  Algeria was a three-way conflict due to the large number of "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pieds-noirs" title="Pieds-noirs">pieds-noirs</a>" (Europeans who had settled there in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_rule_in_Algeria" title="French rule in Algeria">the 125 years of French rule</a>). The political crisis in France caused the collapse of the Fourth Republic, as <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> returned to power in 1958 and finally pulled the French soldiers and settlers out of Algeria by 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a> was replaced in the new 1958 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Constitution_of_1958" title="French Constitution of 1958">Constitution of 1958</a> by the <a href="/wiki/French_Community" title="French Community">French Community</a>. Only <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> refused by referendum to take part in the new colonial organisation. However, the French Community dissolved itself in the midst of the Algerian War; almost all of the other African colonies were granted independence in 1960, following local referendums. Some few colonies chose instead to remain part of France, under the status of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_overseas_departments_and_territories" title="French overseas departments and territories">overseas <i>d&#233;partements</i> (territories)</a>. Critics of <a href="/wiki/Neocolonialism" title="Neocolonialism">neocolonialism</a> claimed that the <i><a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7afrique" title="Fran&#231;afrique">Fran&#231;afrique</a></i> had replaced formal direct rule. They argued that while de Gaulle was granting independence on one hand, he was creating new ties with the help of <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Foccart" title="Jacques Foccart">Jacques Foccart</a>, his counsellor for African matters. Foccart supported in particular the <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_Civil_War" title="Nigerian Civil War">Nigerian Civil War</a> during the late 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Robert Aldrich argues that with Algerian independence in 1962, it appeared that the Empire practically had come to an end, as the remaining colonies were quite small and lacked active nationalist movements. However, there was trouble in French Somaliland (<a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a>), which became independent in 1977. There also were complications and delays in the New Hebrides <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>, which was the last to gain independence in 1980. <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a> remains a special case under French suzerainty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Indian Ocean island of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> voted in referendum in 1974 to retain its link with France and forgo independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>French census statistics from 1931 show an imperial population, outside of France itself, of 64.3 million people living on 11.9 million square kilometers. Of the total population, 39.1 million lived in Africa and 24.5 million lived in Asia; 700,000 lived in the Caribbean area or islands in the South Pacific. The largest colonies were Indochina with 21.5 million (in five separate colonies), Algeria with 6.6 million, Morocco, with 5.4 million, and West Africa with 14.6 million in nine colonies. The total includes 1.9 million Europeans, and 350,000 "assimilated" natives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto;">\n<caption style="font-weight: bold; font-size: 1.1em; margin-bottom: 0.5em"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:French_Empire_1919-1939.png"><img alt="French Empire 1919-1939.png" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="998" decoding="async" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/French_Empire_1919-1939.png/520px-French_Empire_1919-1939.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/French_Empire_1919-1939.png/780px-French_Empire_1919-1939.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3b/French_Empire_1919-1939.png 2x" width="520"/></a> <br/>Population of the French Empire between 1919 and 1939\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th></th>\n<th>&#160;1921&#160;</th>\n<th>&#160;1926&#160;</th>\n<th>&#160;1931&#160;</th>\n<th>&#160;1936&#160;\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">Metropolitan France</a></td>\n<td align="center">39,140,000</td>\n<td align="center">40,710,000</td>\n<td align="center"><b>94,696,000</b></td>\n<td align="center"><b>100,184,000</b></td>\n<td align="center"><b>105,843,000</b></td>\n<td align="center"><b>110,631,000</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center">Percentage of the world population</td>\n<td align="center">5.02%</td>\n<td align="center">5.01%</td>\n<td align="center">5.11%</td>\n<td align="center">5.15%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center" colspan="5"><small>Sources: INSEE,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> SGF<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</small></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_settlers">French settlers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=French_colonial_empire&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: French settlers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Deportation_of_Acadians_order,_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="406" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/170px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/255px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/340px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Deportation_of_Acadians_order,_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The deportation order is read to a group of <a href="/wiki/Acadians" title="Acadians">Acadians</a> in 1755.</div></div></div>\n<p>Unlike elsewhere in Europe, France experienced relatively low levels of emigration to the Americas, with the exception of the <a href="/wiki/Huguenots" title="Huguenots">Huguenots</a> in British or Dutch colonies. France generally had close to the slowest natural population growth in Europe, and emigration pressures were therefore quite small. A small but significant emigration, numbering only in the tens of thousands, of mainly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> French populations led to the settlement of the provinces of <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, Canada and <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a>, both (at the time) French possessions, as well as colonies in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mascarene" title="Mascarene">Mascarene</a> islands and Africa. In New France, Huguenots were banned from settling in the territory, and Quebec was one of the most staunchly Catholic areas in the world until the <a href="/wiki/Quiet_Revolution" title="Quiet Revolution">Quiet Revolution</a>. The current <a href="/wiki/French_Canadians" title="French Canadians">French Canadian</a> population, which numbers in the millions, is descended almost entirely from New France\'s small settler population.\n</p><p>On 31 December 1687 a community of French <a href="/wiki/Huguenots_in_South_Africa" title="Huguenots in South Africa">Huguenots</a> settled in South Africa. Most of these originally settled in the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>, but have since been quickly absorbed into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaner" title="Afrikaner">Afrikaner</a> population. After Champlain\'s founding of Quebec City in 1608, it became the capital of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>. Encouraging settlement was difficult, and while some immigration did occur, by 1763 New France only had a population of some 65,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1787, there were 30,000 white colonists on France\'s colony of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a>. In 1804 <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Dessalines" title="Jean-Jacques Dessalines">Dessalines</a>, the first ruler of an independent Haiti (St. Domingue), ordered the <a href="/wiki/1804_Haiti_massacre" title="1804 Haiti massacre">massacre of whites</a> remaining on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Out of the 40,000 inhabitants on <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>, at the end of the 17th century, there were more than 26,000 blacks and 9,000 whites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Bill Marshall wrote, "The first French effort to colonize <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">Guiana</a>, in 1763, failed utterly when tropical diseases and climate killed all but 2,000 of the initial 12,000 settlers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>French law made it easy for thousands of <i>colons</i>, ethnic or national French from former colonies of North and West Africa, India and <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a> to live in mainland France. It is estimated that 20,000 <i>colons</i> were living in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saigon" title="Saigon">Saigon</a> in 1945. 1.6&#160;million European <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pieds_noirs" title="Pieds noirs">pieds noirs</a></i> migrated from <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, Tunisia and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In just a few months in 1962, 900,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pied-noir" title="Pied-noir">French Algerians</a> left <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> in the largest relocation of population in Europe since <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the 1970s, over 30,000 French <i>colons</i> left <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> regime as the <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a> government confiscated their farms and land properties. In November 2004, several thousand of the estimated 14,000 French nationals in <a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> left the country after days of anti-white violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Apart from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French-Canadians" title="French-Canadians">French-Canadians</a> (<a href="/wiki/French-speaking_Quebecer" title="French-speaking Quebecer">Qu&#233;b&#233;cois</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acadians" title="Acadians">Acadians</a>), <a href="/wiki/Cajuns" title="Cajuns">Cajuns</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people" title="M&#233;tis people">M&#233;tis</a> other populations of French ancestry outside metropolitan France include the <i><a href="/wiki/Caldoche" title="Caldoche">Caldoches</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/New_Caledonia" title="New Caledonia">New Caledonia</a>, the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Zoreilles" title="Zoreilles">Zoreilles</a></i>, <i>Petits-blancs</i> with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franco-Mauritian" title="Franco-Mauritian">Franco-Mauritian</a> of various <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="List of islands in the Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean islands</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beke_people" title="Beke people">Beke people</a> of the French West Indies.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
